The story is science fantasy.  It's depth and meaningfulness are on a par with SuperMan or SpiderMan movies.  It's a blatantly simple good versus evil theme, like in comic books.  But the role of Viveca Lindfors adds some dignity, and one thread of the story has more gratifying depth.<br /><br />The scenery, costumes, actors, and one animal are quite interesting.  (But I had a good laugh at how much this \\"wilderbeast\\" appeared to be propelled in some scenes by two people inside an animal costume!  --It was clearly a low-budget film, but was visually successful anyway.)  The plot is implausible and some details run by in rapid dialogue that's difficult to comprehend or grasp rationally, but you wouldn't expect a fantasy-adventure to be plausible.<br /><br />You'll come away from this movie with a new and entirely novel concept of the Egyptian god Ra.<br /><br />There are two male leads.  One is a young genius who is a linguist/interpreter with special knowledge of ancient hieroglyphics.  He has a lovely guilelessness, and he's the one whom audiences will feel most affection for.  The other male lead is a scary, angry, steely cold, military commander.  When I first saw him and heard him speak I felt such negative vibes coming from him that I thought, \\"I can't stand the bad feelings that this character radiates!  I'm gonna cut off this movie and forget about it!\\" I found I was able to bear with those initial extremely uncomfortable moments, though, and kept watching.  Colonel Jack and other members of the little military squad go through some changes before the storyends.  In the long run, I wasn't sorry that I continued to watch Colonel Jack closely, trying to figure out just what was going on inside his mind and heart. The character profiles of the scientists like Einstein and Borh, humanized them and hit home the thought that these men were more than just the equations they wrote. It was not a child's book, and was written at college level, but with a passion for the subject.<br /><br />Quantum Physics is still in its infantile stages. Everything is so unknown. Imagine Einstein or Gell-Mann in contemporary science with all the right equipment. It was only a theory to them. They spent plenty of time arguing over their theories, but it would take decades just to find some correlation.<br /><br />This book took a subject that was very alien to me, and made me feel at home in a wide-eyed way! 1402270275|5.0|From the very first pages, you enter a world that is both terrifying and exhilarating.  A place so vividly drawn you can practically hear the rustle of silk, feel the grime of smog laden air, and smell the acrid burn of a Spitfire's flames.<br /><br />Plot - Honoria, on the run with a large bounty on her head and two young siblings in tow, heads to the last place anyone would expect - the Whitechapel district.  With all of London under the control of the Echelon Blue Bloods, Whitechapel is a place of last resort - a place of Slasher gangs, soul-crushing poverty, and crime of nightmarish proportions.  A place so terrifying that the villainous Duke of Vickers, a monster hiding his own dark secret, might not enter in pursuit.  Intent on revenge and reacquiring research diaries that may hold a key to curing the Blue Blood virus, Vickers will go to any lengths to get what he wants.<br /><br />Heroine - Honoria Todd is a wonderful character - fiercely independent, strong, and intelligent she has the weight of the world on her small shoulders - at the very least the survival of her younger brother Charlie and sister Lena.  Without resources or even valid papers, her prospects for respectable work are slim and finally gone.  Her agony over the plight her young siblings now find themselves - especially the sickened Charlie - is heartbreaking and genuine.  Her previous lifestyle, though filled with work, had plenty of the finer things in life; clothes, comfortable home and food.  A starving Honoria wonders now if her very life is over when summoned to meet the beast, the devil of Whitechapel - Blade.<br /><br />Hero - Blade, a rogue Blue Blood is a charismatic enigma.  An agonizing past filled with torture, pain and anger, he's a tormented soul that cries out for all the things of a man; work, a family, home, a woman to love.  With all the strength, speed, and cunning intelligence of a predator, Blade is an alpha male to the core and now finds a chance to exact revenge against the man who stole his dreams and destroyed his life - the Duke of Vickers.<br /><br />Romance - began as a slow, smoldering sexual tension that simmered until it erupted into a fireball of passion.  Fighting his own nature and struggling with bouts of rabid jealousy of any male that comes close to Honoria, Blade goes all out to capture her heart.  Having spent a lifetime watching the cat and mouse games that Blue Bloods play, Honoria has no trust nor could put any faith in a Blue Blood.  Blade uses kindness, patience and understanding in a slow dance of seduction that tears through her fear and mistrust.  The love Blade has for his ragtag family is evident and goes a long way in showing Honoria the man he is at heart.<br /><br />I was sorry to leave this place and these people.  I happily look forward to the next book which features Will and perhaps a peak into Blade and Honoria's newfound happiness.  I highly recommend this book to anyone who enjoys heart pounding adventure and swoon worthy romance.
B008S80OU2|5.0|Got this today and I have to say, this is a pretty amazing box set to have.  You get all the Columbia era albums from the debut up through Imaginos plus two discs of rarities and collected tracks from radio broadcasts.<br /><br />There's been some comments about the download site not working.  A few people (myself included) have inquired about this on Eric Bloom's Facebook page and the issue seems to be temporary.  We've been assured that it's being worked on so my advice would be to hold on to the insert with the download code and keep trying or checking back.<br /><br />Back to the music.  The first four albums, Spectres, and Some Enchanted Evening contain the same expanded content from Sony's prior reissues.  On Your Feet..., Mirrors, and everything forward of that has been newly mastered.  Like another reviewer here has said, I will agree and advise to keep your original Sony remastered releases if you want to retain the liner notes, pictures, etc., because the cardboard album sleeve replicas here mostly just replicate the front and back covers and gatefolds when applicable.  The booklet contains a short essay by Lenny Kaye and some great photos and all the song credits.  No lyrics.  So if you want to keep the originals for the liner notes and pics, I'd say keep them but if you're looking to economize, you won't lose the music / video content.<br /><br />It's a great set and if you've been away from the catalog for awhile or are maybe just starting to fall in love with the music, it doesn't get any more complete than this.  BOC - amazing, and hopefully on tour forever!<br /><br />**edit** - as of today, 11/09/12, the download site is live.  Good to go!
